### Section: 12.1 Momentum Transfer:

Momentum transfer is the study of the movement of fluids and the forces that act on them. It is a crucial aspect of transport phenomena as it governs the flow of fluids in chemical processes. In this section, we will discuss the basic principles of momentum transfer and its applications in chemical engineering.

#### 12.1a Newton's Second Law of Motion

Before diving into the specifics of momentum transfer, it is important to understand the fundamental law that governs it: Newton's Second Law of Motion. This law states that the force acting on an object is equal to the mass of the object multiplied by its acceleration. In mathematical terms, it can be expressed as:

$$
F = ma
$$

Where:
- $F$ is the force acting on the object
- $m$ is the mass of the object
- $a$ is the acceleration of the object

This law is essential in understanding the movement of fluids, as it allows us to calculate the forces acting on a fluid and how it will respond to those forces.

#### 12.1b Conservation of Momentum

In addition to Newton's Second Law, the principle of conservation of momentum is also crucial in understanding momentum transfer. This principle states that the total momentum of a closed system remains constant, regardless of any internal changes or external forces acting on the system. In other words, the total momentum before and after an event must be the same.

This principle is particularly important in chemical engineering, as it allows us to predict the behavior of fluids in a system and design processes accordingly. For example, in a chemical reactor, the conservation of momentum can be used to determine the flow rate of reactants and products, ensuring efficient and safe operation.

#### 12.1c Bernoulli's Equation

One of the most well-known equations in fluid mechanics is Bernoulli's equation, which relates the pressure, velocity, and elevation of a fluid in a system. It is based on the principle of conservation of energy and can be expressed as:

$$
P_1 + \frac{1}{2}\rho v_1^2 + \rho gh_1 = P_2 + \frac{1}{2}\rho v_2^2 + \rho gh_2
$$

Where:
- $P$ is the pressure of the fluid
- $\rho$ is the density of the fluid
- $v$ is the velocity of the fluid
- $g$ is the acceleration due to gravity
- $h$ is the elevation of the fluid

Bernoulli's equation is commonly used in the design of pipelines, pumps, and other fluid systems in chemical engineering.

#### 12.1d Applications in Chemical Engineering

Momentum transfer has numerous applications in chemical engineering, including the design and operation of pumps, compressors, and turbines. It is also crucial in understanding the behavior of fluids in pipes, reactors, and other process equipment. By applying the principles of momentum transfer, engineers can optimize processes, troubleshoot problems, and ensure the safe and efficient operation of chemical processes.

### Section: 12.2 Heat Transfer:

Heat transfer is the study of the transfer of thermal energy between systems. It is a vital aspect of transport phenomena as it plays a crucial role in the design and operation of chemical processes. In this section, we will discuss the basic principles of heat transfer and its applications in chemical engineering.

#### 12.2a Modes of Heat Transfer

There are three main modes of heat transfer: conduction, convection, and radiation. Conduction is the transfer of heat through a solid or stationary fluid, while convection is the transfer of heat through the movement of fluids. Radiation is the transfer of heat through electromagnetic waves. In chemical engineering, all three modes of heat transfer can occur simultaneously and must be considered in the design and operation of processes.

#### 12.2b Fourier's Law of Heat Conduction

Similar to Newton's Second Law of Motion, Fourier's Law of Heat Conduction is a fundamental law in heat transfer. It states that the rate of heat transfer through a material is directly proportional to the temperature gradient and the cross-sectional area of the material, and inversely proportional to its thickness. Mathematically, it can be expressed as:

$$
q = -kA\frac{dT}{dx}
$$

Where:
- $q$ is the heat transfer rate
- $k$ is the thermal conductivity of the material
- $A$ is the cross-sectional area
- $dT/dx$ is the temperature gradient

#### 12.2c Heat Exchangers

Heat exchangers are essential components in many chemical processes, as they allow for the efficient transfer of heat between two fluids. They can be classified into three main types: parallel flow, counterflow, and crossflow. The design and operation of heat exchangers require a thorough understanding of heat transfer principles.

#### 12.2d Applications in Chemical Engineering

Heat transfer has numerous applications in chemical engineering, including the design and operation of heat exchangers, reactors, and distillation columns. It is also crucial in the control of temperature in processes, as well as in the production of energy and chemicals. By understanding the principles of heat transfer, engineers can optimize processes, improve energy efficiency, and ensure the safe operation of chemical processes.

### Section: 12.3 Mass Transfer:

Mass transfer is the movement of substances from one location to another. It is a crucial aspect of transport phenomena as it plays a significant role in the separation and purification of chemicals in chemical processes. In this section, we will discuss the basic principles of mass transfer and its applications in chemical engineering.

#### 12.3a Fick's Law of Diffusion

Fick's Law of Diffusion is a fundamental law in mass transfer, which describes the rate of diffusion of a substance through a medium. It states that the rate of diffusion is directly proportional to the concentration gradient and the diffusion coefficient of the substance. Mathematically, it can be expressed as:

$$
J = -D\frac{dC}{dx}
$$

Where:
- $J$ is the mass flux
- $D$ is the diffusion coefficient
- $dC/dx$ is the concentration gradient

Fick's Law of Diffusion is essential in understanding the movement of substances in chemical processes, such as in the separation of components in a mixture.

#### 12.3b Mass Transfer Coefficient

The mass transfer coefficient is a measure of the efficiency of mass transfer between two phases, such as a gas and a liquid. It is affected by factors such as the physical properties of the substances, the geometry of the system, and the flow conditions. In chemical engineering, the mass transfer coefficient is crucial in the design and operation of separation processes, such as distillation and absorption.

#### 12.3c Applications in Chemical Engineering

Mass transfer has numerous applications in chemical engineering, including the design and operation of separation processes, such as distillation, absorption, and extraction. It is also crucial in the production of chemicals, such as in the purification of raw materials and the removal of impurities. By understanding the principles of mass transfer, engineers can optimize processes, improve product quality, and ensure the safe operation of chemical processes.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have covered the basic principles of transport phenomena, including momentum transfer, heat transfer, and mass transfer. We have discussed the fundamental laws and equations that govern these processes and their applications in chemical engineering. It is essential to have a strong understanding of these concepts to design and operate chemical processes efficiently and safely. In the next chapter, we will delve deeper into the topic of transport phenomena and explore more advanced concepts and applications.


### Introduction

In this chapter, we will be discussing the topic of transport phenomena in chemical engineering. Transport phenomena refers to the study of how mass, momentum, and energy are transferred in a system. This is a fundamental concept in chemical engineering as it plays a crucial role in the design and operation of chemical processes. Understanding transport phenomena is essential for engineers to optimize processes, troubleshoot problems, and develop new technologies.

The study of transport phenomena can be divided into three main areas: fluid mechanics, heat transfer, and mass transfer. Fluid mechanics deals with the motion of fluids and the forces that act on them. Heat transfer involves the transfer of thermal energy between systems. Mass transfer is the movement of substances from one location to another. These three areas are interconnected and often occur simultaneously in chemical processes.

In this chapter, we will cover the basic principles of transport phenomena, including the governing equations and their applications. We will also discuss the different types of transport processes and their significance in chemical engineering. Additionally, we will explore the different methods used to analyze and solve transport phenomena problems, such as analytical and numerical techniques.

It is important to note that transport phenomena is a complex and interdisciplinary subject, involving principles from physics, chemistry, and mathematics. Therefore, a strong foundation in these areas is necessary to fully understand and apply the concepts discussed in this chapter. With that in mind, let us dive into the world of transport phenomena and explore its importance in chemical engineering.

### Section: 12.1 Momentum Transfer:

Momentum transfer is the study of the movement of fluids and the forces that act on them. It is a crucial aspect of transport phenomena as it governs the flow of fluids in chemical processes. In this section, we will discuss the basic principles of momentum transfer and its applications in chemical engineering.

#### 12.1a Newton's Second Law and Conservation of Momentum

The foundation of momentum transfer lies in Newton's Second Law, which states that the net force acting on an object is equal to the product of its mass and acceleration. In the context of fluid mechanics, this law can be applied to a small volume of fluid, known as a control volume, to determine the forces acting on it.

In addition to Newton's Second Law, the principle of conservation of momentum is also crucial in understanding momentum transfer. This principle states that the total momentum of a system remains constant unless acted upon by an external force. In other words, the momentum of a fluid entering a control volume must be equal to the momentum leaving the control volume, taking into account any external forces acting on the system.

#### 12.1b Fluid Flow and Bernoulli's Equation

The study of momentum transfer also involves the analysis of fluid flow. Fluid flow can be classified into two types: laminar and turbulent. Laminar flow occurs when the fluid particles move in a smooth, orderly manner, while turbulent flow is characterized by chaotic, irregular motion.

One of the most important equations in fluid mechanics is Bernoulli's equation, which relates the pressure, velocity, and elevation of a fluid in a steady flow. This equation is based on the principle of conservation of energy and is often used to analyze fluid flow in pipes and other systems.

#### 12.1c Applications in Chemical Engineering

Momentum transfer plays a crucial role in many chemical engineering processes, such as mixing, pumping, and filtration. For example, in a mixing tank, momentum transfer is responsible for the movement of fluid particles and the mixing of different components. In a pump, momentum transfer is used to increase the pressure and flow rate of a fluid. In filtration, momentum transfer is involved in the movement of particles through a filter medium.

### Section: 12.2 Heat Transfer:

Heat transfer is the study of the transfer of thermal energy between systems. It is an essential aspect of transport phenomena as it affects the temperature and phase changes of substances in chemical processes. In this section, we will discuss the basic principles of heat transfer and its applications in chemical engineering.

#### 12.2a Modes of Heat Transfer

There are three main modes of heat transfer: conduction, convection, and radiation. Conduction is the transfer of heat through a solid or stationary fluid, while convection is the transfer of heat through the movement of a fluid. Radiation is the transfer of heat through electromagnetic waves.

#### 12.2b Fourier's Law and Heat Transfer Coefficient

The rate of heat transfer is governed by Fourier's Law, which states that the rate of heat transfer is proportional to the temperature gradient and the cross-sectional area of the system. The proportionality constant is known as the heat transfer coefficient and is dependent on the properties of the material and the mode of heat transfer.

#### 12.2c Applications in Chemical Engineering

Heat transfer is a crucial aspect of many chemical engineering processes, such as distillation, evaporation, and heat exchangers. In distillation, heat transfer is used to separate different components of a mixture based on their boiling points. In evaporation, heat transfer is used to remove water from a solution to concentrate the desired product. Heat exchangers are used to transfer heat between two fluids at different temperatures, such as in a chemical reactor.

### Section: 12.3 Mass Transfer:

Mass transfer is the movement of substances from one location to another. It is a fundamental aspect of transport phenomena as it affects the concentration and purity of substances in chemical processes. In this section, we will discuss the basic principles of mass transfer and its applications in chemical engineering.

#### 12.3a Diffusion and Fick's Law

The movement of substances in mass transfer is governed by diffusion, which is the random movement of particles from an area of high concentration to an area of low concentration. Fick's Law describes the rate of diffusion and states that it is proportional to the concentration gradient and the diffusion coefficient of the substance.

#### 12.3b Convective Mass Transfer

In addition to diffusion, mass transfer can also occur through convection, which is the movement of a fluid caused by a difference in density. This can be seen in processes such as distillation, where the vapor phase carries the substance to be separated from one location to another.

#### 12.3c Applications in Chemical Engineering

Mass transfer is a crucial aspect of many chemical engineering processes, such as absorption, extraction, and crystallization. In absorption, mass transfer is used to remove a gas from a mixture by dissolving it into a liquid. In extraction, mass transfer is used to separate a desired substance from a mixture by transferring it to a different solvent. In crystallization, mass transfer is involved in the formation of crystals from a solution.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have discussed the three main areas of transport phenomena: fluid mechanics, heat transfer, and mass transfer. We have explored the basic principles and equations governing each area and their applications in chemical engineering processes. It is important to have a strong understanding of transport phenomena to effectively design and operate chemical processes. In the next chapter, we will delve deeper into the topic of fluid mechanics and its applications in chemical engineering.


### Introduction

In this chapter, we will be discussing the topic of transport phenomena in chemical engineering. Transport phenomena refers to the study of how mass, momentum, and energy are transferred in a system. This is a fundamental concept in chemical engineering as it plays a crucial role in the design and operation of chemical processes. Understanding transport phenomena is essential for engineers to optimize processes, troubleshoot problems, and develop new technologies.

The study of transport phenomena can be divided into three main areas: fluid mechanics, heat transfer, and mass transfer. Fluid mechanics deals with the motion of fluids and the forces that act on them. Heat transfer involves the transfer of thermal energy between systems. Mass transfer is the movement of substances from one location to another. These three areas are interconnected and often occur simultaneously in chemical processes.

In this chapter, we will cover the basic principles of transport phenomena, including the governing equations and their applications. We will also discuss the different types of transport processes and their significance in chemical engineering. Additionally, we will explore the different methods used to analyze and solve transport phenomena problems, such as analytical and numerical techniques.

It is important to note that transport phenomena is a complex and interdisciplinary subject, involving principles from physics, chemistry, and mathematics. Therefore, a strong foundation in these areas is necessary to fully understand and apply the concepts discussed in this chapter. With that in mind, let us dive into the world of transport phenomena and explore its importance in chemical engineering.

### Section: 12.1 Momentum Transfer:

Momentum transfer is the study of the movement of fluids and the forces that act on them. It is a crucial aspect of transport phenomena as it governs the flow of fluids in chemical processes. In this section, we will discuss the basic principles of momentum transfer, including the equations that govern it and its applications in chemical engineering.

#### 12.1a Newton's Second Law of Motion

The foundation of momentum transfer lies in Newton's Second Law of Motion, which states that the force acting on an object is equal to the mass of the object multiplied by its acceleration. In the context of fluid mechanics, this law can be applied to the movement of fluids, where the force acting on the fluid is equal to the mass of the fluid multiplied by its acceleration.

#### 12.1b Conservation of Momentum

In addition to Newton's Second Law, the principle of conservation of momentum is also crucial in understanding momentum transfer. This principle states that the total momentum of a closed system remains constant, meaning that the sum of the momenta of all the objects in the system remains the same. In the context of fluid mechanics, this means that the total momentum of a fluid remains constant unless acted upon by an external force.

#### 12.1c Applications in Chemical Engineering

Momentum transfer plays a significant role in chemical engineering, particularly in the design and operation of chemical processes. For example, in the design of pipelines and pumps, engineers must consider the forces acting on the fluid and the resulting pressure drop to ensure efficient and safe transport of fluids. In addition, momentum transfer is also crucial in mixing and agitation processes, where the movement of fluids is essential for achieving proper mixing and reaction rates.

### Section: 12.2 Heat Transfer:

Heat transfer is the study of the transfer of thermal energy between systems. It is another important aspect of transport phenomena in chemical engineering, as it affects the temperature and energy balance of chemical processes. In this section, we will discuss the basic principles of heat transfer and its applications in chemical engineering.

#### 12.2a Modes of Heat Transfer

There are three main modes of heat transfer: conduction, convection, and radiation. Conduction is the transfer of heat through a solid or stationary fluid, while convection is the transfer of heat through the movement of fluids. Radiation is the transfer of heat through electromagnetic waves. In chemical engineering, all three modes of heat transfer can occur simultaneously and must be considered in the design and operation of processes.

#### 12.2b Governing Equations

The governing equations for heat transfer are the Fourier's Law of Conduction, Newton's Law of Cooling, and the Stefan-Boltzmann Law of Radiation. These equations describe the rate of heat transfer and the temperature gradient between two systems. In chemical engineering, these equations are used to calculate the heat transfer rates and design heat exchangers for efficient heat transfer.

#### 12.2c Applications in Chemical Engineering

Heat transfer is a crucial aspect of chemical engineering, as it affects the efficiency and safety of chemical processes. For example, in distillation processes, heat transfer is essential for separating different components based on their boiling points. In addition, heat transfer is also crucial in reactor design, where the temperature must be carefully controlled to ensure optimal reaction rates and product quality.

### Section: 12.3 Mass Transfer:

Mass transfer is the movement of substances from one location to another. It is a fundamental aspect of transport phenomena in chemical engineering, as it affects the composition and purity of products in chemical processes. In this section, we will discuss the basic principles of mass transfer and its applications in chemical engineering.

#### 12.3a Diffusion

Diffusion is the movement of molecules from an area of high concentration to an area of low concentration. This process is driven by the random motion of molecules and is crucial in mass transfer. In chemical engineering, diffusion is used in processes such as gas absorption, where a gas is transferred from one phase to another.

#### 12.3b Mass Transfer Coefficients

Mass transfer coefficients are used to describe the rate of mass transfer between two phases. These coefficients take into account factors such as the concentration gradient, diffusivity, and interfacial area. In chemical engineering, mass transfer coefficients are used to design equipment such as distillation columns and absorption towers.

#### 12.3c Interphase Mass Transfer

Interphase mass transfer refers to the transfer of mass between two phases, such as gas-liquid or liquid-liquid systems. This process is crucial in many chemical processes, such as extraction and absorption. In chemical engineering, engineers must consider the interphase mass transfer rates to design efficient and cost-effective processes.

### Conclusion:

In this chapter, we have discussed the three main areas of transport phenomena: fluid mechanics, heat transfer, and mass transfer. We have explored the basic principles and governing equations of each area and their applications in chemical engineering. It is important to note that these areas are interconnected and often occur simultaneously in chemical processes. Therefore, a thorough understanding of transport phenomena is crucial for chemical engineers to design and operate efficient and safe processes. In the next chapter, we will delve deeper into the topic of fluid mechanics and its applications in chemical engineering.

In this chapter, we have explored the fundamental principles of transport phenomena in chemical engineering. We have discussed the three main types of transport: mass, momentum, and energy, and how they are interconnected in various processes. We have also delved into the mathematical models and equations used to describe these phenomena, such as Fick's law, Navier-Stokes equations, and Fourier's law. By understanding these concepts, chemical engineers can design and optimize processes to achieve efficient and effective transport of materials and energy.

One key takeaway from this chapter is the importance of considering all three types of transport in any chemical engineering process. Neglecting one type can lead to inefficiencies and potential hazards. Additionally, we have seen how transport phenomena play a crucial role in various industries, from pharmaceuticals to food processing to energy production. As chemical engineers, it is our responsibility to apply these principles to solve real-world problems and contribute to the advancement of society.

By mastering these concepts and equations, readers will be well-equipped to tackle more complex topics in the field. ## Chapter: - Chapter 13: Chemical Engineering Design:

### Introduction

Welcome to the thirteenth chapter of "Integrated Chemical Engineering I: A Comprehensive Guide". In this chapter, we will be discussing the topic of Chemical Engineering Design. This is a crucial aspect of chemical engineering that involves the application of scientific and engineering principles to design, develop, and optimize processes for the production of various products. 

Chemical engineering design is a complex and multidisciplinary field that requires a deep understanding of various subjects such as thermodynamics, transport phenomena, reaction kinetics, and process control. It involves the use of mathematical models, computer simulations, and experimental data to design and optimize processes that are safe, efficient, and cost-effective.

In this chapter, we will cover various topics related to chemical engineering design, including process synthesis, process flow diagrams, equipment design, and process optimization. We will also discuss the importance of sustainability and safety in the design process and how to incorporate these factors into the design of chemical processes.

It is important to note that chemical engineering design is an ongoing process that involves continuous improvement and adaptation. Therefore, this chapter will provide a foundation for understanding the fundamental principles of chemical engineering design, but it is essential to continue learning and staying updated with the latest advancements in the field.

Now, let's dive into the world of chemical engineering design and explore the various aspects and challenges of this fascinating field. 


### Section: 13.1 Process Design:

Chemical engineering design is the process of creating and optimizing processes for the production of various products. It involves the application of scientific and engineering principles to design, develop, and improve processes that are safe, efficient, and cost-effective. In this section, we will discuss the key aspects of process design and its importance in chemical engineering.

#### 13.1a Process Flow Diagrams (PFDs)

Process flow diagrams (PFDs) are graphical representations of the process design that show the flow of materials and energy through a chemical process. They are an essential tool in chemical engineering design as they provide a visual representation of the process and its components. PFDs are typically the first step in the design process and are used to communicate the process design to other engineers, operators, and stakeholders.

PFDs consist of various symbols and notations that represent different process components such as equipment, pipes, valves, and instruments. These symbols are standardized and follow specific guidelines to ensure consistency and clarity in communication. PFDs also include important information such as process conditions, material flow rates, and energy balances.

The creation of PFDs involves a thorough understanding of the process and its components. It requires the use of mathematical models, experimental data, and engineering principles to accurately represent the process. PFDs are continuously updated and refined throughout the design process as more information becomes available.

In addition to being a communication tool, PFDs also serve as a basis for further design and analysis. They can be used to identify potential issues and optimize the process design. PFDs are also crucial in the development of process control strategies and safety measures.

In conclusion, process flow diagrams are an essential aspect of process design in chemical engineering. They provide a visual representation of the process and serve as a basis for further design and analysis. As such, it is crucial for chemical engineers to have a thorough understanding of PFDs and their role in the design process. 


### Section: 13.1 Process Design:

Chemical engineering design is the process of creating and optimizing processes for the production of various products. It involves the application of scientific and engineering principles to design, develop, and improve processes that are safe, efficient, and cost-effective. In this section, we will discuss the key aspects of process design and its importance in chemical engineering.

#### 13.1a Process Flow Diagrams (PFDs)

Process flow diagrams (PFDs) are graphical representations of the process design that show the flow of materials and energy through a chemical process. They are an essential tool in chemical engineering design as they provide a visual representation of the process and its components. PFDs are typically the first step in the design process and are used to communicate the process design to other engineers, operators, and stakeholders.

PFDs consist of various symbols and notations that represent different process components such as equipment, pipes, valves, and instruments. These symbols are standardized and follow specific guidelines to ensure consistency and clarity in communication. PFDs also include important information such as process conditions, material flow rates, and energy balances.

The creation of PFDs involves a thorough understanding of the process and its components. It requires the use of mathematical models, experimental data, and engineering principles to accurately represent the process. PFDs are continuously updated and refined throughout the design process as more information becomes available.

In addition to being a communication tool, PFDs also serve as a basis for further design and analysis. They can be used to identify potential issues and optimize the process design. PFDs are also crucial in the development of process control strategies and safety measures.

### Subsection: 13.1b Piping and Instrumentation Diagrams (P&IDs)

Piping and Instrumentation Diagrams (P&IDs) are another important tool in chemical engineering design. They are more detailed than PFDs and provide a more comprehensive view of the process. P&IDs include information about the piping layout, equipment specifications, and control systems.

Similar to PFDs, P&IDs use standardized symbols and notations to represent different components of the process. However, P&IDs also include additional information such as pipe sizes, valve types, and instrument tags. This level of detail allows for a more accurate representation of the process and aids in the design and construction of the actual plant.

The creation of P&IDs requires a thorough understanding of the process and its components, as well as knowledge of piping and instrumentation design principles. P&IDs are continuously updated and refined throughout the design process, and they serve as a crucial reference for engineers, operators, and maintenance personnel.

In conclusion, Piping and Instrumentation Diagrams are an essential aspect of process design in chemical engineering. They provide a more detailed and accurate representation of the process, aiding in the design, construction, and operation of chemical plants. 


### Section: 13.1 Process Design:

Chemical engineering design is a crucial aspect of the field, as it involves the creation and optimization of processes for the production of various products. It requires the application of scientific and engineering principles to design, develop, and improve processes that are safe, efficient, and cost-effective. In this section, we will discuss the key aspects of process design and its importance in chemical engineering.

#### 13.1a Process Flow Diagrams (PFDs)

Process flow diagrams (PFDs) are graphical representations of the process design that show the flow of materials and energy through a chemical process. They are an essential tool in chemical engineering design as they provide a visual representation of the process and its components. PFDs are typically the first step in the design process and are used to communicate the process design to other engineers, operators, and stakeholders.

PFDs consist of various symbols and notations that represent different process components such as equipment, pipes, valves, and instruments. These symbols are standardized and follow specific guidelines to ensure consistency and clarity in communication. PFDs also include important information such as process conditions, material flow rates, and energy balances.

The creation of PFDs involves a thorough understanding of the process and its components. It requires the use of mathematical models, experimental data, and engineering principles to accurately represent the process. PFDs are continuously updated and refined throughout the design process as more information becomes available.

In addition to being a communication tool, PFDs also serve as a basis for further design and analysis. They can be used to identify potential issues and optimize the process design. PFDs are also crucial in the development of process control strategies and safety measures.

### Subsection: 13.1b Piping and Instrumentation Diagrams (P&IDs)

Piping and Instrumentation Diagrams (P&IDs) are another important tool in chemical engineering design. They are more detailed than PFDs and provide a more comprehensive representation of the process. P&IDs include information about the process equipment, piping, instrumentation, and control systems.

Similar to PFDs, P&IDs use standardized symbols and notations to represent different components of the process. However, P&IDs also include additional information such as pipe sizes, valve types, and instrument specifications. This level of detail allows for a more accurate representation of the process and aids in the design and operation of the process.

P&IDs are typically created after the PFDs and are used to further refine the process design. They are also crucial in the development of process control strategies and safety measures. P&IDs are continuously updated and refined throughout the design process as more information becomes available.

### Subsection: 13.1c Process Simulation

Process simulation is a powerful tool in chemical engineering design that allows for the virtual testing and optimization of a process. It involves the use of mathematical models and computer software to simulate the behavior of a process under various conditions. Process simulation can be used to predict the performance of a process, identify potential issues, and optimize the process design.

The process simulation software uses mathematical models to represent the physical and chemical processes occurring in the system. These models take into account factors such as mass and energy balances, reaction kinetics, and thermodynamic properties. By inputting process conditions and parameters, the software can simulate the behavior of the process and provide valuable insights into its performance.

Process simulation is an essential tool in chemical engineering design as it allows for the evaluation of different process designs and operating conditions without the need for physical experimentation. This saves time and resources and allows for a more efficient and cost-effective design process. Process simulation is continuously used throughout the design process to refine and optimize the process design.

In conclusion, process design is a crucial aspect of chemical engineering that involves the creation and optimization of processes for the production of various products. PFDs, P&IDs, and process simulation are all important tools in the design process, providing valuable insights and aiding in the development of safe, efficient, and cost-effective processes. 


### Section: 13.2 Equipment Design:

Chemical engineering design involves the creation and optimization of processes for the production of various products. However, the design of equipment is equally important as it directly affects the efficiency and safety of the process. In this section, we will discuss the key aspects of equipment design and its role in chemical engineering.

#### 13.2a Design of Reactors

Reactors are essential components in chemical processes as they facilitate the desired chemical reactions. The design of reactors involves selecting the appropriate type of reactor, determining the optimal operating conditions, and sizing the reactor to meet the process requirements.

##### Types of Reactors

There are several types of reactors used in chemical processes, including batch, continuous stirred-tank, plug flow, and packed bed reactors. Each type has its advantages and limitations, and the selection of the appropriate reactor depends on the specific process requirements.

##### Operating Conditions

The operating conditions of a reactor, such as temperature, pressure, and residence time, play a crucial role in determining the efficiency and selectivity of the desired reaction. These conditions are often determined through experimentation and mathematical modeling to optimize the process.

##### Sizing of Reactors

The size of a reactor is determined by the desired production rate and the kinetics of the reaction. It is essential to consider factors such as heat transfer, mass transfer, and pressure drop when sizing a reactor to ensure its efficient operation.

The design of reactors also involves considering safety measures, such as the use of appropriate materials and the incorporation of safety features, to prevent accidents and ensure the well-being of operators.

In conclusion, the design of reactors is a crucial aspect of chemical engineering design, and it requires a thorough understanding of the process and its requirements. The selection of the appropriate type of reactor, determination of optimal operating conditions, and sizing of the reactor are all essential in ensuring the success of a chemical process. 


### Section: 13.2 Equipment Design:

Chemical engineering design involves the creation and optimization of processes for the production of various products. However, the design of equipment is equally important as it directly affects the efficiency and safety of the process. In this section, we will discuss the key aspects of equipment design and its role in chemical engineering.

#### 13.2a Design of Reactors

Reactors are essential components in chemical processes as they facilitate the desired chemical reactions. The design of reactors involves selecting the appropriate type of reactor, determining the optimal operating conditions, and sizing the reactor to meet the process requirements.

##### Types of Reactors

There are several types of reactors used in chemical processes, including batch, continuous stirred-tank, plug flow, and packed bed reactors. Each type has its advantages and limitations, and the selection of the appropriate reactor depends on the specific process requirements.

Batch reactors are commonly used for small-scale production and are characterized by a fixed volume and a single batch of reactants. Continuous stirred-tank reactors (CSTRs) are used for large-scale production and have a continuous flow of reactants and products. Plug flow reactors (PFRs) are ideal for reactions with a high degree of conversion and are characterized by a plug-like flow of reactants through the reactor. Packed bed reactors are used for reactions involving solid catalysts and have a fixed bed of catalyst particles through which the reactants flow.

##### Operating Conditions

The operating conditions of a reactor, such as temperature, pressure, and residence time, play a crucial role in determining the efficiency and selectivity of the desired reaction. These conditions are often determined through experimentation and mathematical modeling to optimize the process.

Temperature is a critical factor in determining the rate of a chemical reaction. As temperature increases, the rate of reaction also increases due to the higher kinetic energy of the reactant molecules. However, too high of a temperature can lead to unwanted side reactions or even thermal runaway, which can be dangerous. Pressure also affects the rate of reaction, as it can influence the equilibrium of the reaction. Residence time, or the amount of time the reactants spend in the reactor, is also important as it determines the extent of conversion and the selectivity of the desired product.

##### Sizing of Reactors

The size of a reactor is determined by the desired production rate and the kinetics of the reaction. It is essential to consider factors such as heat transfer, mass transfer, and pressure drop when sizing a reactor to ensure its efficient operation.

Heat transfer is crucial in maintaining the desired temperature for the reaction. This can be achieved through the use of heat exchangers or by controlling the flow rate of the reactants. Mass transfer is important for reactions involving gas-liquid or liquid-liquid phases, as it affects the rate of reaction and the distribution of reactants and products. Pressure drop, or the decrease in pressure as the reactants flow through the reactor, must also be considered to ensure the reactor can handle the desired flow rate.

The design of reactors also involves considering safety measures, such as the use of appropriate materials and the incorporation of safety features, to prevent accidents and ensure the well-being of operators.

In conclusion, the design of reactors is a crucial aspect of chemical engineering design, and it requires a thorough understanding of the process and its requirements. The selection of the appropriate type of reactor, determination of optimal operating conditions, and proper sizing are all essential for the successful design and operation of a chemical process. 


### Section: 13.2 Equipment Design:

Chemical engineering design involves the creation and optimization of processes for the production of various products. However, the design of equipment is equally important as it directly affects the efficiency and safety of the process. In this section, we will discuss the key aspects of equipment design and its role in chemical engineering.

#### 13.2a Design of Reactors

Reactors are essential components in chemical processes as they facilitate the desired chemical reactions. The design of reactors involves selecting the appropriate type of reactor, determining the optimal operating conditions, and sizing the reactor to meet the process requirements.

##### Types of Reactors

There are several types of reactors used in chemical processes, including batch, continuous stirred-tank, plug flow, and packed bed reactors. Each type has its advantages and limitations, and the selection of the appropriate reactor depends on the specific process requirements.

Batch reactors are commonly used for small-scale production and are characterized by a fixed volume and a single batch of reactants. Continuous stirred-tank reactors (CSTRs) are used for large-scale production and have a continuous flow of reactants and products. Plug flow reactors (PFRs) are ideal for reactions with a high degree of conversion and are characterized by a plug-like flow of reactants through the reactor. Packed bed reactors are used for reactions involving solid catalysts and have a fixed bed of catalyst particles through which the reactants flow.

##### Operating Conditions

The operating conditions of a reactor, such as temperature, pressure, and residence time, play a crucial role in determining the efficiency and selectivity of the desired reaction. These conditions are often determined through experimentation and mathematical modeling to optimize the process.

Temperature is a critical factor in determining the rate of a chemical reaction. As temperature increases, the rate of reaction also increases due to the higher kinetic energy of the reactant molecules. However, too high of a temperature can lead to unwanted side reactions or even thermal runaway, which can be dangerous. Pressure is another important factor, as it can affect the equilibrium of the reaction and the solubility of reactants. Residence time, or the amount of time the reactants spend in the reactor, is also crucial as it determines the extent of the reaction and the yield of the desired product.

#### 13.2b Design of Separation Equipment

Separation equipment is used to separate different components of a mixture based on their physical or chemical properties. This is an essential step in many chemical processes, as it allows for the isolation and purification of the desired product. The design of separation equipment involves selecting the appropriate type of equipment, determining the operating conditions, and sizing the equipment to meet the process requirements.

##### Types of Separation Equipment

There are various types of separation equipment used in chemical processes, including distillation columns, centrifuges, filters, and membranes. Each type has its advantages and limitations, and the selection of the appropriate equipment depends on the specific process requirements.

Distillation columns are commonly used for separating liquid mixtures based on their boiling points. Centrifuges are used for separating solid-liquid mixtures by spinning the mixture at high speeds, causing the heavier components to settle at the bottom. Filters are used for separating solid particles from a liquid or gas stream. Membranes are used for separating components based on their size or molecular weight.

##### Operating Conditions

The operating conditions of separation equipment depend on the type of equipment and the properties of the mixture being separated. For example, in a distillation column, the temperature and pressure must be carefully controlled to achieve the desired separation. In a centrifuge, the speed and duration of spinning must be optimized to achieve efficient separation. In all cases, the operating conditions must be carefully chosen to ensure the desired product is obtained.

#### 13.2c Design of Heat Exchangers

Heat exchangers are essential equipment in chemical processes as they transfer heat between two fluids at different temperatures. The design of heat exchangers involves selecting the appropriate type of exchanger, determining the optimal operating conditions, and sizing the exchanger to meet the process requirements.

##### Types of Heat Exchangers

There are several types of heat exchangers used in chemical processes, including shell and tube, plate and frame, and double pipe exchangers. Each type has its advantages and limitations, and the selection of the appropriate exchanger depends on the specific process requirements.

Shell and tube exchangers are the most commonly used type and consist of a shell with multiple tubes inside. The hot and cold fluids flow through the shell and tubes, respectively, allowing for efficient heat transfer. Plate and frame exchangers have multiple plates with small channels for the fluids to flow through, providing a large surface area for heat transfer. Double pipe exchangers consist of two pipes, one inside the other, with the hot and cold fluids flowing in opposite directions.

##### Operating Conditions

The operating conditions of a heat exchanger, such as the flow rate, temperature, and pressure of the fluids, play a crucial role in determining the efficiency of heat transfer. These conditions are often determined through experimentation and mathematical modeling to optimize the process. Additionally, the choice of materials for the exchanger must also be carefully considered to ensure compatibility with the fluids and to prevent corrosion or fouling.


### Section: 13.3 Safety and Hazard Analysis:

Chemical engineering design not only involves creating efficient and effective processes, but also ensuring the safety of those processes. In this section, we will discuss the importance of safety and hazard analysis in chemical engineering design.

#### 13.3a Hazard Identification

Before any chemical process can be designed, it is crucial to identify potential hazards that may arise during its operation. This involves a thorough understanding of the chemicals and reactions involved, as well as the equipment and operating conditions.

One method of hazard identification is through a Hazard and Operability (HAZOP) study. This involves a team of experts analyzing the process and identifying potential deviations from normal operating conditions that could lead to hazards. Another method is through a Failure Modes and Effects Analysis (FMEA), which focuses on identifying potential failures in equipment and their potential consequences.

Once hazards have been identified, they must be evaluated and prioritized based on their severity and likelihood of occurrence. This allows for the implementation of appropriate safety measures to mitigate or eliminate the hazards.

#### 13.3b Risk Assessment

After hazards have been identified and evaluated, a risk assessment must be conducted to determine the level of risk associated with each hazard. This involves considering the severity of the consequences, the likelihood of the hazard occurring, and the effectiveness of existing safety measures.

One commonly used method of risk assessment is the Risk Matrix, which plots the likelihood and severity of a hazard on a matrix to determine the level of risk. Another method is the Layer of Protection Analysis (LOPA), which involves identifying layers of protection and their effectiveness in mitigating the risk associated with a hazard.

#### 13.3c Safety Measures

Based on the results of the risk assessment, appropriate safety measures must be implemented to reduce the risk associated with hazards. These measures can include engineering controls, such as designing equipment with safety features, administrative controls, such as implementing safety procedures and training, and personal protective equipment (PPE).

It is important to note that safety measures should not only be implemented during the design phase, but also continuously evaluated and improved upon throughout the life of the process.

#### 13.3d Emergency Response Plan

In addition to implementing safety measures, it is crucial to have an emergency response plan in place in case of an accident or incident. This plan should include procedures for responding to different types of emergencies, as well as training for employees on how to handle these situations.

#### 13.3e Regulatory Compliance

Chemical engineering design must also comply with various regulations and standards to ensure the safety of the process and the environment. These regulations may include occupational safety and health standards, environmental regulations, and industry-specific guidelines.

In conclusion, safety and hazard analysis are essential components of chemical engineering design. By identifying hazards, conducting risk assessments, implementing safety measures, and having an emergency response plan in place, we can ensure the safe operation of chemical processes. 


### Section: 13.3 Safety and Hazard Analysis:

#### 13.3c Safety Measures

These measures may include engineering controls, such as the use of safety equipment and design modifications, administrative controls, such as standard operating procedures and training, and personal protective equipment for workers.

In addition to these measures, it is important to regularly review and update safety protocols to account for any changes in the process or equipment. This can help to prevent accidents and ensure the continued safety of workers and the surrounding environment.

#### 13.3d Case Study: Bhopal Disaster

One of the most well-known chemical engineering disasters is the Bhopal disaster, which occurred in 1984 in Bhopal, India. A gas leak from a pesticide plant resulted in the release of toxic gases, causing the deaths of thousands of people and long-term health effects for many more.

This disaster serves as a tragic reminder of the importance of safety and hazard analysis in chemical engineering design. It highlights the need for thorough hazard identification, risk assessment, and implementation of appropriate safety measures to prevent such catastrophic events from occurring.

In response to the Bhopal disaster, stricter safety regulations and protocols were implemented in the chemical industry, emphasizing the importance of safety in all stages of chemical engineering design.

### Section: 13.3 Safety and Hazard Analysis:

Chemical engineering design not only involves creating efficient and effective processes, but also ensuring the safety of those processes. In this section, we will discuss the importance of safety and hazard analysis in chemical engineering design.

#### 13.3a Hazard Identification

Before any chemical process can be designed, it is crucial to identify potential hazards that may arise during its operation. This involves a thorough understanding of the chemicals and reactions involved, as well as the equipment and operating conditions.

One method of hazard identification is through a Hazard and Operability (HAZOP) study. This involves a team of experts analyzing the process and identifying potential deviations from normal operating conditions that could lead to hazards. Another method is through a Failure Modes and Effects Analysis (FMEA), which focuses on identifying potential failures in equipment and their potential consequences.

Once hazards have been identified, they must be evaluated and prioritized based on their severity and likelihood of occurrence. This allows for the implementation of appropriate safety measures to mitigate or eliminate the hazards.

#### 13.3b Risk Assessment

After hazards have been identified and evaluated, a risk assessment must be conducted to determine the level of risk associated with each hazard. This involves considering the severity of the consequences, the likelihood of the hazard occurring, and the effectiveness of existing safety measures.

One commonly used method of risk assessment is the Risk Matrix, which plots the likelihood and severity of a hazard on a matrix to determine the level of risk. Another method is the Layer of Protection Analysis (LOPA), which involves identifying layers of protection and their effectiveness in mitigating the risk associated with a hazard.

#### 13.3c Safety Measures and Procedures

Based on the results of the risk assessment, appropriate safety measures and procedures must be implemented to ensure the safe operation of the chemical process. These measures may include engineering controls, administrative controls, and personal protective equipment.

Engineering controls involve designing the process and equipment in a way that minimizes the potential for hazards. This may include using automated systems, implementing safety interlocks, and using materials that are less hazardous.

Administrative controls involve establishing procedures and protocols for safe operation, such as regular maintenance and inspections, proper training for operators, and emergency response plans.

Personal protective equipment (PPE) is the last line of defense and should be used in conjunction with engineering and administrative controls. PPE may include items such as gloves, goggles, and respirators, and should be selected based on the specific hazards present in the process.

It is important to regularly review and update safety measures and procedures to ensure they are effective and up-to-date with current industry standards. Additionally, all personnel involved in the operation of the chemical process should be trained on these measures and procedures to ensure their proper implementation.

In conclusion, safety and hazard analysis is a crucial aspect of chemical engineering design. By identifying hazards, conducting risk assessments, and implementing appropriate safety measures and procedures, we can ensure the safe and efficient operation of chemical processes. 


### Section: 13.4 Economic Analysis:

Chemical engineering design not only involves creating efficient and effective processes, but also ensuring that these processes are economically viable. In this section, we will discuss the importance of economic analysis in chemical engineering design.

#### 13.4a Capital Cost Estimation

Before a chemical process can be implemented, it is necessary to estimate the capital cost required for its construction. This involves determining the cost of equipment, materials, labor, and other expenses associated with building and commissioning the process.

One method of capital cost estimation is through the use of cost indexes, which track the changes in cost of materials and equipment over time. Another method is through the use of process simulation software, which can provide a detailed breakdown of the cost of each component in the process.

#### 13.4b Operating Cost Estimation

In addition to capital costs, it is also important to estimate the operating costs of a chemical process. This includes the cost of raw materials, energy, labor, maintenance, and other expenses associated with running the process.

One method of operating cost estimation is through the use of process simulation software, which can provide a detailed breakdown of the cost of each component in the process. Another method is through the use of historical data and industry benchmarks to estimate the cost of raw materials and energy.

#### 13.4c Profitability Analysis

After estimating the capital and operating costs, a profitability analysis must be conducted to determine the financial viability of the process. This involves calculating the net present value (NPV), internal rate of return (IRR), and payback period of the project.

One commonly used method for profitability analysis is through the use of discounted cash flow (DCF) analysis, which takes into account the time value of money. Another method is through the use of sensitivity analysis, which evaluates the impact of changing key variables on the profitability of the project.

#### 13.4d Optimization for Cost Reduction

Once the economic analysis has been completed, it is important to optimize the process design to reduce costs and increase profitability. This can involve redesigning certain aspects of the process, such as using alternative materials or equipment, or optimizing operating conditions.

One method of optimization is through the use of process integration techniques, which aim to minimize energy and material usage in a process. Another method is through the use of process intensification, which involves designing processes that are more compact and efficient.

In conclusion, economic analysis is a crucial aspect of chemical engineering design, as it ensures that processes are not only efficient and safe, but also financially viable. By estimating capital and operating costs, conducting profitability analysis, and optimizing the process design, chemical engineers can create processes that are both technically and economically sound.


### Section: 13.4 Economic Analysis:

Chemical engineering design not only involves creating efficient and effective processes, but also ensuring that these processes are economically viable. In this section, we will discuss the importance of economic analysis in chemical engineering design.

#### 13.4a Capital Cost Estimation

Before a chemical process can be implemented, it is necessary to estimate the capital cost required for its construction. This involves determining the cost of equipment, materials, labor, and other expenses associated with building and commissioning the process.

One method of capital cost estimation is through the use of cost indexes, which track the changes in cost of materials and equipment over time. This method takes into account the inflation and deflation of costs, as well as any changes in technology that may affect the cost of equipment. Another method is through the use of process simulation software, which can provide a detailed breakdown of the cost of each component in the process. This method allows for a more accurate estimation of costs, as it takes into account specific equipment and materials needed for the process.

#### 13.4b Operating Cost Estimation

In addition to capital costs, it is also important to estimate the operating costs of a chemical process. This includes the cost of raw materials, energy, labor, maintenance, and other expenses associated with running the process.

One method of operating cost estimation is through the use of process simulation software, which can provide a detailed breakdown of the cost of each component in the process. This method allows for a more accurate estimation of costs, as it takes into account specific equipment and materials needed for the process. Another method is through the use of historical data and industry benchmarks to estimate the cost of raw materials and energy. This method may be less accurate, but can provide a general idea of operating costs based on past data and industry standards.

#### 13.4c Profitability Analysis

After estimating the capital and operating costs, a profitability analysis must be conducted to determine the financial viability of the process. This involves calculating the net present value (NPV), internal rate of return (IRR), and payback period of the project.

One commonly used method for profitability analysis is through the use of discounted cash flow (DCF) analysis, which takes into account the time value of money. This method calculates the present value of future cash flows and compares it to the initial investment to determine the profitability of the project. Another method is through the use of sensitivity analysis, which evaluates the impact of changing variables on the profitability of the project. This method can help identify potential risks and uncertainties that may affect the financial success of the project.

In conclusion, economic analysis is a crucial aspect of chemical engineering design. It allows engineers to determine the feasibility and profitability of a process, and make informed decisions about the design and implementation of chemical processes. By considering both capital and operating costs, as well as conducting a profitability analysis, engineers can ensure that their designs are not only efficient and effective, but also economically viable.


### Section: 13.4 Economic Analysis:

Chemical engineering design not only involves creating efficient and effective processes, but also ensuring that these processes are economically viable. In this section, we will discuss the importance of economic analysis in chemical engineering design and how it can be used to evaluate the profitability of a process.

#### 13.4a Capital Cost Estimation

Before a chemical process can be implemented, it is necessary to estimate the capital cost required for its construction. This involves determining the cost of equipment, materials, labor, and other expenses associated with building and commissioning the process.

One method of capital cost estimation is through the use of cost indexes, which track the changes in cost of materials and equipment over time. This method takes into account the inflation and deflation of costs, as well as any changes in technology that may affect the cost of equipment. Another method is through the use of process simulation software, which can provide a detailed breakdown of the cost of each component in the process. This method allows for a more accurate estimation of costs, as it takes into account specific equipment and materials needed for the process.

#### 13.4b Operating Cost Estimation

In addition to capital costs, it is also important to estimate the operating costs of a chemical process. This includes the cost of raw materials, energy, labor, maintenance, and other expenses associated with running the process.

One method of operating cost estimation is through the use of process simulation software, which can provide a detailed breakdown of the cost of each component in the process. This method allows for a more accurate estimation of costs, as it takes into account specific equipment and materials needed for the process. Another method is through the use of historical data and industry benchmarks to estimate the cost of raw materials and energy. This method may be less accurate, but can provide a general idea of operating costs based on past data and industry standards.

#### 13.4c Profitability Analysis

Once the capital and operating costs have been estimated, it is important to evaluate the profitability of the chemical process. This involves comparing the expected revenue generated by the process to the total cost of construction and operation.

One method of profitability analysis is through the use of net present value (NPV) calculations. This takes into account the time value of money and calculates the present value of all future cash flows associated with the process. A positive NPV indicates that the process is profitable, while a negative NPV indicates that the process is not economically viable.

Another method is through the use of internal rate of return (IRR) calculations. This measures the rate of return on the initial investment and compares it to the cost of capital. A higher IRR indicates a more profitable process.

In addition to these methods, sensitivity analysis can also be used to evaluate the impact of changing variables, such as raw material costs or market demand, on the profitability of the process.

In conclusion, economic analysis is a crucial aspect of chemical engineering design. It allows engineers to evaluate the feasibility and profitability of a process before it is implemented, and can help guide decision making throughout the design process. By considering both capital and operating costs, as well as using various methods of profitability analysis, engineers can ensure that their designs are not only efficient and effective, but also economically viable.

We have discussed the importance of understanding the process and its requirements, as well as the various tools and techniques used in the design process. We have also touched upon the different stages of design, from conceptualization to detailed design, and the role of simulation and optimization in the process. By the end of this chapter, you should have a solid understanding of the key principles and considerations involved in chemical engineering design.

### Exercises
#### Exercise 1
Consider a chemical process that produces a desired product at a rate of 100 kg/hr. The process has a conversion efficiency of 80% and a yield of 90%. Calculate the amount of raw material required to produce 1 ton of the desired product.

#### Exercise 2
Design a heat exchanger for a process that requires cooling from 80C to 40C. The process stream has a flow rate of 500 L/min and a specific heat capacity of 4.2 kJ/kgK. The cooling water stream has a flow rate of 1000 L/min and a specific heat capacity of 4.18 kJ/kgK. Assume a heat transfer coefficient of 500 W/mK.

#### Exercise 3
Using the McCabe-Thiele method, determine the number of theoretical stages required for the separation of a binary mixture with a feed composition of 40% A and 60% B. The distillate composition is 90% A and the bottom composition is 10% A. Assume constant molal overflow and a reflux ratio of 2.

#### Exercise 4
Design a pump for a process that requires a flow rate of 1000 L/min and a pressure increase of 5 bar. The pump efficiency is 80% and the specific gravity of the fluid is 0.8. Assume a pump speed of 1500 rpm and a specific speed of 100.

#### Exercise 5
Using Aspen Plus, simulate a distillation column for the separation of a binary mixture with a feed composition of 30% A and 70% B. The distillate composition is 90% A and the bottom composition is 10% A. Compare the results with the theoretical calculations from Exercise 3.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the fundamentals of chemical engineering design. We have discussed the importance of understanding the process and its requirements, as well as the various tools and techniques used in the design process. We have also touched upon the different stages of design, from conceptualization to detailed design, and the role of simulation and optimization in the process. By the end of this chapter, you should have a solid understanding of the key principles and considerations involved in chemical engineering design.
